I am disappointed by the service I received especially after reading so many other favorable reviews of this place.

Recently, my bag with my Prius key was stolen. I had my boyfriend call A+ Security Lock and Key to get a quote (reviews at other dealerships suggest women are charged higher quotes so I had him call to avoid potential issues).

They informed him it would be $85 for a vehicle lockout to open the door to the car. When they sent their servicer over (30 mins later, very punctual) to open the car door, he told me that it would be $240 to open the car door. I asked him why this was nearly 3x the quote given to my boyfriend. He tried to explain to me that it would have been easier to open the car door if the key were inside the car???

After speaking to his supervisor, the service man again told me it would be $240 to OPEN THE CAR and another $300 for the chip key. After some back and forth haggling, the servicer agreed to lower the fee to *open the car* to $150 because of a "Google discount" (lol) - i.e. using Google and not Yelp - complete nonsense. I then spoke to his supervisor  who informed me that my boyfriend had not told him that I needed a new key and that I just needed to get back into my car. I still asked why it would be so expensive to open my car to which I did not get a clear answer. I again asked the service man why it would be easier to open the car door if the key were inside. Can someone explain this to me?

After some haggling (I don't remember all the details) the supervisor informed me that he would put me in contact with a different "ignitioner" to assess the scenario and give me a quote. When I talked to the different ignitioner (Ben, he was perfectly nice and reasonable) I explained how they initially quoted my boyfriend $85 and then saw me and tried to charge me $240 to just open the door - no key!! He said he was very sorry about the situation and would give them a call and I could expect a new quote. The supervisor called back and said that he could get the door open a get me a new smart key for $285 total. I don't know if this is a good price but considering it was half of what they were initially trying to charge I accepted.

After Ben arrived, there were no issues at all - he got the door open in 2 minutes (he did not seem bothered that there was no key inside).  I had a new key in about 20 minutes. Thanks Ben - you're a cool guy.</text>

Love this historic hotel that is central to everything on Venice Beach! Very clean, great firm queen bed (pull out sofa bed should only be for young kids as it is not very sturdy).  Bathroom is small but tub is big, and has a more modern feel, no mold or dirtiness at all.

Water pressure is awesome, fridge works great and all appliances are awesome for a longer stay.

This is a gem with the amazing views, I would only recommend the ocean view it is well worth the slight up charge!

Staff is great, and u have anything u need just outside the doors.<//Text>

Awful experience. I would avoid this place at all cost. Drove in from central California to stay one night on our way home to CO. We called the hotel repeatedly for an hour straight while driving in circles in Venice trying to find where to park, with no one answering the phone. Finally got through to someone and was immediately put on hold.  This hotel is in the middle of the delirious circus that is Venice beach, and parking/driving is a literal nightmare. I'm not quite sure how this place expects to run a business without answering 1/100 phone calls. If you aren't going to answer questions via phone then maybe try PUTING INFORMATION ABOUT PARKING ON YOUR WEBSITE.

After finally getting info on where to park, we came back to the hotel to find our bags locked in the office, with a 'will return' sign on the door. We had no room keys, no bags, no change of clothes, and had to wait outside the office until the front desk guy got back from his coffee break. After driving in LA traffic all day the last thing I want to do is drive in circles to park, and then sit and wait to get into a room while front desk guy takes a break.

The beds are horrifically uncomfortable, and the noise is unparalleled. The area around the hotel is filthy and dangerous, requiring an almost constant police presence at night. We could literally hear police radios all night while they searched for a suspect. The drone of radios was frequently punctuated with loud rap music and screaming bums at 3:00 AM. <Response>None<//Response><user_name>Rise Up Studios< /user_name><rating>5<//rating>< Text>
Absolutely beautiful hike with gorgeous views of the surrounding landscape. I went on a cloudy day and made it almost all the way to the top before walking into a cloud.

The first mile is a steep windy forest trail and the last three miles are on an access road that leads up to the communication towers at the top. The views from the access road are spectacular.<//Text>

<review>Late winter is the best time to do this hike for sure, (February/7/2021).
I was started from Valley hiking up to North Peak, South Peak of Mount Saint Helena.(4,343ft).
My hike was between 10 to 11 miles round trip, and about 2,300 ft of the elevation gain.
No entrance fee, but parking is limited, and a couple of small turnouts on the side of the road.
It has several picnic tables at the trailhead.
My beautiful hike started out with pleasantly through forest.
And just under a mile into the trail, I came across a monument Robert Louis Stevenson Memorial marks.
The trail continues with the Bubble Wall, where rock climbers trying to practice their climbing skills.
Following with graded fire road for the rest of my hike  up to the summit of North Peak.
It is steep but butterflies leading me the way, made its so doable.
The 360 degrees views are spectacular, truly breathtaking.
I was spending sometimes at North Peak to enjoyed my lunch, soaked into the phenomenally views, and capturing a lot of pictures...
The magnificent view keeps getting better and better.
From the top of the summit.
I was able to see Mount shasta 200 miles from the  North, Napa and Sonoma Counties with vineyards and rolling hills from the West, and I can see Mount Diablo  peaking its head up through the clouds. The Sierra Crest, glistening in white, and a thin outline of Mount Lassen.
On the way down, I was explored the Silverado Mine. Highly recommended everyone should check it out!
There are some interesting rocks formations at the Mine.
75 percent of my hike was exposed to the sun. ( bring full liter of water and sunscreen, hat if you can keep it on your head).
Wear good hiking boots for support and for traction.
Finally, don‚Äôt wait until summer.
It is worthwhile!< /review></record>

<Review>Difficulty: Moderate (due to distance, but elevation gain- easy)
Mileage: ~10 miles
Pets: No dogs
View: Wine country, ocean on a clear day
What to bring: (In winter) At least 1-2 liters, snacks, hat, jacket, gloves
Parking: Highway 29
Fee: free
Time: ~3-5 hours

We came on 12/28. It was so cold. We started the hike at 7:30, the sun was hidden behind rain clouds and the wind was super strong. We summited in 1 hour and 50 minutes and it was so windy at the top. So bad that we literally summited then descended 1 minute later. Couldn‚Äôt even chill at the top. We hit some slight snow. It was sprinkling but it was so cold, slight snow came down. We thought it was pollen until more came down and it made my jacket wet. It didn‚Äôt stick much but it was pretty horrible. I thought my fingers were going to fall off. The view was still amazing, sort of gloomy but the sun started to come out once we went down. The first .8 miles is thru the woods, probably the hardest part of the 10 mile hike. The rest was super easy up a big well paved fire road. Didn‚Äôt run into anyone going up. We finished in 3 hours with slightly jogging on and off down. Definitely recommend this hike. If I lived in area would probably use it to trail run.< /Review>< Pictures>

<text>VERY LONG AND DIFFICULT. Online this is rated as difficult, 9.3 miles long and 2,099' elevation gain from the trail head to the top. But this trail is a nice trail through a forest in the beginning then a fire access/utility/logging road to the top. The trail/road is pretty steep and it's really hard to go uphill the whole way and then downhill all the way back. The last mile was torture! There's nice views though and it can get windy but it's nice and refreshing if you're hot. Make sure if you're starting this trail that you have 4+ hours of day light! You don't want to be stumbling around on the rocks in the dark. You can take the access road all the way back to the main road but it's longer and comes out pretty far south of the trailhead I believe. And bring water! No one should be going up there without water. There's also not that much trash up there either, but I guess that's because a difficult trail keeps out those that litter.</text></record>

< Review>
A great place to hike. The Mt. Saint Helena Summit is about a five mile hike and the first mile is single track trail and the remaining four miles is open fire road. Due to the trail being a 10 mile round trip it will take you 3-4 hours to complete and due to recent fires there is very little to no shade on the hike. Bring water and start early to avoid the heat from Spring to Fall.<//Review>
</record>
</dataset><record>
<text>Did not realize how popular this hike was. I don't think I could do it again though. It is definitely worth it though. We went before 8 AM in case the lot was full, but thankfully it wasn't. We parked in the lot in front of the table rock trail and crossed the street to the Mt. St. Helena Trailhead. I would advise being careful going up through the woods before you get to the road. Even with our hiking shoes, my husband and I slipped a few times and I eventually fell pretty hard.

Take lots of water, Gatorades, snacks. You will definitely need it. I wouldn't skimp on any of those items.<//text><date>1592252189582<//date>< UserId.>

<Review>BRING SUNSCREEN

For mother's day, I took my mom to hike the trail and when we left our home we were in a thick cold fog bank. Freezing cold, and unsure of what lat ahead, we left our warm weather clothes in the car. About 2 1/2 miles up the trail, if you go on a foggy day, you break above the fog bank. We were we damp from fog, but relieved to be in sudden 90¬∞ weather. Hiking in sports bras, we enjoyed the rest our day. The following morning we woke to pain and red skin. If you do this hike don't forget to lather in sunscreen because you won't feel it in the moment, but your skin will!< /Review>< pictures>

< Review>
Time to update my review for Serenity.

Given the great prices, I decided to come back
4 more times since my last review.

While I will maintain that the type of massage (both the pattern and style) continue to be varied rather than cohesive to just "Thai" - the quality has gotten a lot better and more consistent.

Each of the last 4 massages could be described as - Good / Good / Great / and Excellent! The last massage was done by Lucy (forgive me if I got that incorrect).

She was fantastic overall - and made 90minutes feel too short because the massage was so great.

I still struggle with 2 things: turnover - I never know who will be there when I go. And the beds. The beds are comfortable enough but the hole where you place tour head is too rigid and too small - so either your sinus above your brow or your jaw takes a lot of the weight and becomes unbearable over time.

Fix this last issue and 5*s can be yours! Ill be back. Thankfully!< /Review>

< review>
I've purchased two cars from this dealer before.  Both times with Tevis as the front person.  She's awesome, even if she does call soda 'pop'.

As car buying goes it couldn't really be any simpler or less pressure.  Find the car you want on their website and they will have it waiting at the lot that's nearest to you, or if you don't like the one that they have they'll go and get the one you want.  In my case, the car I wanted looked black on the web page but was dark brown at the lot.  It was exactly what I wanted other than the color, but they never even tried to convince me or my wife to accept it (eg: hey we'll knock X dollars off, or other tactics I've seen elsewhere),  insisting that we should be happy with our selection.

The prices are good compared to anywhere else and the test drive is, not kidding here: Seven days long.  It's a full week long test drive with a no bones policy about bringing the car back at any time for an exchange or just if you change your mind.  The final price for the car is completely explained, and I didn't see any padding type expenses like 'paperwork preparation' or 'detailing fees' or anything like that which I have seen at other locations.  They have options you can select like extended warranties, lojack installation etc that you're welcome to chose or skip, and it's in a take out menu format so you can pick and chose what you prefer rather than selecting from a 'good better best' type list.

As I said the prices and vehicle quality are comparable to elsewhere, so the real reason for choosing this place over another is in the details of the purchasing experience.  On the whole I feel like this is pretty much what the car buying experience should look and feel like.</review>

< review>
In April 2011 we purchased a 1 year old 2010 Hyundai Elantra from Enterprise. The purchase experience was sub-par, but I attribute that to the inexperience of the associate helping us. The price was reasonable and on par with what our research showed for a 1 year old car in excellent condition with 30K miles and a clean carfax report.

Unfortunately, as we found out in 2015 when we went to trade it in, instead of the approximately $7000 it should have been worth, it was only worth $3500. The carfax report showed it had been in a serious accident in March 2011. Enterprise, as the owner of this former rental car, knew full well that it had been in an accident and doubtless intentionally dumped it on us at full price knowing that carfax would not have been updated yet to show the accident. They essentially scammed us out of $3500. This is not just a problem with the Reseda location, but rather with the ethics of Enterprise Used Car Sales as a whole, because the car was transferred from a lot in Arizona.

I advise staying away from Enterprise. They are no better than any other shady used car seller.<//review>

< Review>
My first time there, not impressed one bit. The prices were fine, the quantity was okay, but the ingredients were lacking. I had the fettuccine Alfredo with shrimp and it's made either from a flower or cornstarch gravy, seriously lacking cheese... not to mention the lack of heavy cream and butter. That's no way to make Alfredo sauce. The shrimp, while somewhat adequate in size and quantity, were boiled, not saut√©ed in butter and garlic. They were most likely purchased frozen and already boiled. And the meal didn't come with any sides - no side salad, no bread, nothing. Just a plate of noodles, shrimp, and gravy - that wasn't very good. And the noodles were overdone. I think the cooks need to understand the term Al dente. The wateress wasn't much better. She didn't offer a side salad, and we sat there for over 20 minutes waiting for her to come over and ask if we wanted dessert, which we did. And no grated cheese was offered.< /Review>

<Name>Michael Doyle<//Name><review>Fugazzis Restaurant is a corner property on the main drag in Visalia. It is an upbeat, slightly upscale, establishment where Audrey and I chose to spend about 90 minutes to enjoy a nice, full meal.  We split a Mediterranean salad, an encrusted salmon fillet and a side of coconut prawns.  She finally settled upon a Ruffino Prosecco (fruit-forward sparkling white wine) while I enjoyed a Corona Extra (on tap) with lime.  Two bread varieties were tabled at the outset with an oil, white balsamic and red pepper dipping sauce.  The wait staff were relaxed, pleasant and professional.  The table setting, location and style were well suited for a trendy, Italian bistro.  The food was fresh, texture and temperature appropriate in every course.  The  presentation was above average, the flavors subtle, yet challenging.   We paid $50.55 + our generous gratuity for a dining experience well done.</review>< time>

My wife and I love this place. This is our favorite local spot in Visalia. Catch it in the evening, and plan to have great drinks, great food, and great service!
Great portions, reasonably priced for a fancy restaurant.
